â”‚ Analyzing the provider card refactor. The changes eliminate 11 platform-specific card components (BlueskyCard, FbPageCard, FbUserCard, GoogleCard, InstagramCard, LinkedInCard, MastodonCard, PinterestCard, ThreadsCard, TikTokCard, YouTubeCard) and replace them with a unified GenericProviderCard that uses configuration from providerCards.ts. However, BaseProviderCard expects `platformType`, not `platform`. Looking at line 2, it explicitly passes `:platform-type="config.platformType"`, which correctly maps platform â†’ platformType. This is good, but `platform` will also be passed through $props. This creates a redundant/unknown prop warning. Need to verify if this causes issues.   â”‚

â”‚ Second potential issue: BaseProviderCard.vue has a retry mechanism with computedAsync. The retryLoad function (line 220-226) sets error to undefined, resets retryCount, sets loading to true, and calls fetchAccountData(). However, there's a problem: computedAsync is already managing the loading state and the async computation. When retryLoad manually calls fetchAccountData(), it doesn't actually trigger the computedAsync to re-evaluate. The accountData computed is only re-evaluated when its dependencies change. This means the manual retry button might not work correctly.   â”‚

â”‚ Third potential issue: In MultiProviderCard.vue, the event handler changed from `@selected="handleAccountSelection"` to `@update:selected="handleAccountSelection(account)"`. This is a breaking change in the event signature. The old platform cards emitted a `selected` event, but now with v-model:selected in BaseProviderCard, it emits `update:selected`. Need to check if handleAccountSelection expects the account object or just the account ID, and whether the event payload changed.   â”‚

â”‚ CRITICAL BUG FOUND: In MultiProviderCard.vue, the event handler changed from `@selected="handleAccountSelection"` to `@update:selected="handleAccountSelection(account)"`. However, v-model:selected emits boolean values (true/false) when the selection state changes, NOT the account object. The handleAccountSelection function expects an OAuthAccount object (line 144), but it will receive a boolean instead. This will cause runtime errors when trying to access account.$id on a boolean value.   â”‚

â”‚ Wait, I need to reconsider. The old platform cards used `defineModel<boolean>("selected")` which creates a v-model prop. But the old MultiProviderCard listened to @selected (not @update:selected). Since v-model emits "update:selected", the @selected listener would never fire in the old code either. This means the selection feature was ALREADY broken in main branch! The new code tries to fix it by using @update:selected, but incorrectly passes account instead of handling the boolean value. This is a pre-existing bug that the refactor attempted to fix but introduced a new bug.   â”‚

â”‚ CRITICAL BUG CONFIRMED: In CompletionView.vue line 50, `@update:selected="toggleAccountStatus(account)"` receives a boolean from v-model:selected, but toggleAccountStatus (line 334-336) expects an OAuthAccount and tries to access account.active. When the event fires, it will pass true/false to toggleAccountStatus, causing `boolean.active = !boolean.active` which will either fail silently or throw "Cannot create property 'active' on boolean 'true'". This breaks the account selection feature completely.   â”‚

â”‚ Now analyzing the BaseProviderCard retry mechanism. In BaseProviderCard.vue lines 214-218, accountData is a computedAsync that calls fetchAccountData. The retryLoad function (lines 220-226) manually calls fetchAccountData() but this doesn't trigger the computedAsync to re-evaluate. computedAsync only re-evaluates when its dependencies change (mounted.value or props.accountId). Simply calling fetchAccountData() won't update accountData.value. The retry button will not work as intended.   â”‚

â”‚ Analyzing the GenericProviderCard v-bind="$props" issue. Line 2 uses `v-bind="$props"` which spreads all props including `platform`. Then it explicitly passes `:platform-type="config.platformType"`. This means BaseProviderCard receives both `platform` (unknown prop) and `platformType` (expected prop). This will cause Vue warnings "Unknown prop: platform" but won't break functionality since BaseProviderCard only uses platformType.   â”‚
